<td class="postcell">
<div>
    <div class="post-text" itemprop="text">

<p>I'm trying to save a webpage as text file, using the following function:</p>

<pre><code>def html_to_txt(): 
    import urllib.request 
    url = str(input('Enter URL: ')) 
    page = urllib.request.urlopen(url) 
    with open(str(input('Enter filename: ')), "w") as f: 
        for x in page: 
            f.write(str(x).replace('\\n','\n')) 
    s= 'Done' 
    return s
</code></pre>

<p>It gives a correct output, that means I can save a given webpage. But, the final text file contains a <code>b'</code> before the very first line, and a <code>'b'</code> before each following line.</p>

<p>Here's a sample output of my function (taken from: <code>http://www.uniprot.org/uniprot/P57052.txt</code>)</p>

<pre><code>$ cat P57052.txt
b'ID   RBM11_HUMAN             Reviewed;         281 AA.
'b'AC   P57052; Q6YNC2; Q8NBA1; Q8NFF6;
'b'DT   01-DEC-2000, integrated into UniProtKB/Swiss-Prot.
'b'DT   01-DEC-2000, sequence version 1.
'b'DT   09-JUL-2014, entry version 111.
'b'DE   RecName: Full=Splicing regulator RBM11;
'b'DE   AltName: Full=RNA-binding motif protein 11;
'b'GN   Name=RBM11;
</code></pre>

<p>I wonder if it has something to do with binary file "default", I mean, if the webpage is  automatically saved with binary features by my python script.</p>

<p>Thanks in advance for your review.</p>

<a name="58018"></a>
<div id="answer-58018" class="answer accepted-answer" data-answerid="58018"  itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer" itemprop="acceptedAnswer">
    <table>
        <tr>
            <td class="votecell">
                

<div class="vote">
        <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="58018">
        <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a>
        <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">2</span>
        <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a>



        <span class="vote-accepted-on load-accepted-answer-date" title="loading when this answer was accepted...">accepted</span>

</div>

            </td>
            


<td class="answercell">
    <div class="post-text" itemprop="text">
<p>As a review, the code needs some work with regard separation of concerns. A single function shouldn't get user input, get a URL and write to a file. If you try to write unit tests for it, you'll quickly see it's better to split the functionality.</p>

<p>With regard to the problem, try something as follows:</p>

<pre><code>import urllib2

url = 'http://www.uniprot.org/uniprot/P57052.txt'
response = urllib2.urlopen(url)
with open('output.txt', 'w') as f:
    f.write(response.read())
</code></pre>

<p>I hope this helps.</p>
    </div>

    window.ads_library.initialized = true;

          setTargeting: function() {},

      };

      $('.ads').hide();
      $('.ad-srp-inline').hide();
      $('.facet-bar').attr('data-offset-top', '48px');
      pbjs = function() {
        return {
          refreshAds: function() {}
        };
      };
      return false;
    }
    return true;
  };
